  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_93647a58-8d55-48d5-8fdc-3b7d72688f3a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText11562405316782603457" style="display:none">Dreaming of the dead might mean a restless night for anyone, but for Nina Grey it was a warning. <br /><br />Still healing from her last run-in with Hell, Nina struggles with not only her life as a Brown University student, but also as an intern at Titan Shipping, her father's company. Recurring nightmares about her father's violent death have become a nightly event, but being overwhelmed with guilt from Ryan's unexpected departure to the Armed Forces, and heart ache over Claire being across the ocean to protect him, Nina believes her sleepless nights are the least of her problems—but she's wrong.<br /><br />Worried about Nina's declining health, Jared must steal back Shax's book for answers. Fighting new enemies, and with the help of new friends, Jared's worst fear comes to fruition. Desperate, he is faced with a choice: Fight Hell alone, or start a war with Heaven.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18131691718234697859">Also Found On: <a href='http://abookandarecord.blogspot.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Book and A Record</a><br/><br/>Requiem was a really good follow up. I felt like Requiem took the perfect spot as the middle book in a trilogy, it wrapped up nearly everything that happened in Providence, while setting up a strong background for what I assume will happen in Eden. So, what I liked about Requiem:<br/>1. Jared. Question: will I ever get over Jared. Answer: No.<br/>2. Claire. I have to admit, I really just love the Ryel family. Jared, Claire, and Bex are all such well rounded characters wit</span>
  <span id="freeText18131691718234697859" style="display:none">Also Found On: <a href="http://abookandarecord.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">A Book and A Record</a><br /><br />Requiem was a really good follow up. I felt like Requiem took the perfect spot as the middle book in a trilogy, it wrapped up nearly everything that happened in Providence, while setting up a strong background for what I assume will happen in Eden. So, what I liked about Requiem:<br />1. Jared. Question: will I ever get over Jared. Answer: No.<br />2. Claire. I have to admit, I really just love the Ryel family. Jared, Claire, and Bex are all such well rounded characters with such surprising personalities. I really enjoyed Claire stepping forward into the spotlight in this one. Her interactions with Ryan were also so hilarious, and the straightforwardness gives such a breath of fresh air compared to Jared’s drawn out explanations.<br />3. Beth. Beth is basically the best, best friend a girl could ask for. She just accepts Nina for who she is, and accepts all of her excuses for not being at work (and they are good excuses). She understands Nina’s job probably better than Nina does (like any fantastic assistant/bff) And she is such a great balance for Nina’s personality. Rarely does she have any massive freak out moments. <br />4. The dreams. They added just what I wanted for this story, a little bit of heart pounding mystery. Anyone who knows me knows that I scare easy, and these night terrors of Nina’s really made my heart go double time. It’s also nice whenever I get to see Gabe. Jared, being one of my favorite characters, seems to take a lot from his dad, so getting to see the way Gabe acted/reacted was pretty awesome. Also, there is another someone that has dreams from Gabe and I found that little tidbit to be cute and heartbreaking all at once. Love.<br />What I had a hard time with in this one.<br />1. It still felt like Nina was a little bit hung up on Ryan. I understand that she feels bad about certain choices he makes, but girlfriend, come on. You’re hurting your fiancé over a dude that is kind of a jerk, and also a consenting adult who is old enough to make his own decisions. It’s strange because in Providence, I felt like Ryan didn’t have a chance, however in Requiem the Nina/Ryan relationship somehow seemed stronger (at least in the beginning).<br />2. Sasha. Sasha felt like a bulk character to me. I kept waiting for her to do something truly heinous (involving Shax or another demon) but she didn’t. As a matter of fact she kind of faded into the background, maybe she’ll have a bigger role in Eden? Who knows, but in this one she was kind of a loose cannon and my mind kept wandering to what she would do next instead of focusing on the story at hand.<br />All in all, I really enjoyed Requiem, as I mentioned before it fulfills the duty held by most middle books in a trilogy, and reads similar to Providence (though I felt Providence was a sort of whirlwind, and Requiem was a little more peaceful pacing-wise) Although there were some scenes in which I kind of lost some steam (being in the middle east, I just really don’t like Ryan with Nina. Ugh.) Again, four pies because I’m literally hungering to get my hands on Eden!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18131691718234697859" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_348712956" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/348712956" />
    <a title="Kimmy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6797622-kimmy"><img alt="Kimmy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326111991p2/6797622.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/348712956?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kimmy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kimmy" href="/user/show/6797622-kimmy">Kimmy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer348712956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5323416329188777819">If I were in an alternate universe, I think I would have really liked to get into Brown University. According to this book, you don't need o study, <i>ever</i>, you can go MIA in some other country for a few months and come back to resume studies like nothing ever happened and no questions asked, and you can be one serious demon ass-kicker and still get a four-point-oh GPA without even trying. <br/><br/>Either that or the characters in the story must be really smart. <i>Freaking smart. Like some Einstein genius. As</i></span>
  <span id="freeText5323416329188777819" style="display:none">If I were in an alternate universe, I think I would have really liked to get into Brown University. According to this book, you don't need o study, <i>ever</i>, you can go MIA in some other country for a few months and come back to resume studies like nothing ever happened and no questions asked, and you can be one serious demon ass-kicker and still get a four-point-oh GPA without even trying. <br /><br />Either that or the characters in the story must be really smart. <i>Freaking smart. Like some Einstein genius. As if their smartness is so freaking.</i> <br /><br />Funny, from Nina's actions when it comes to saving the world and preserving the delicate balance between heaven and hell, it seems to me otherwise - that she is just one big helpless bimbo, who needs saving all the time.<br /><br />Besides Nina, Jared is also one unlikable character. A highly-paid personal bodyguard/babysitter/stalker/personal slave, Jared seems to never tire of Nina's antics and whiny demands. But Jared himself is one whiny fella too, with some serious needy clingy issues. Which girl would ever want a guy who needs someone to boost his ego 24/7 by assuring that he is the girl's pretty bouncy bubbly bunny boy? Eck.<br /><br />Nevertheless, I gave this book a rather high rating because despite listening to the characters scrounging and complaining about being apart for even two days and making out, I found Requiem mildly entertaining. Some parts were a bit scary too. Like when someone with supersharp senses says, "They're coming!" (if you can guess what they refers to), it really heightens the suspense as the characters who are in the middle of something try to flee from "them". Get the picture?<br /><br />If you are slightly interested in Requiem but put off by my review, I implore you to reconsider - read Requiem but for the sake of Claire. She is pow-wow awesome! Claire brings the definition of bad-ass to a whole new level. She fights, plays with guns, is ruthless and competitive, somewhat elusive when it comes to boys (fangirling!), can knock out the boys (including Jared) anytime, and that she had to work doubly hard initially to gain recognition as she was a girl should make Claire all the more idolized by female folks. Moreover, I love the fact that she too had moments of weakness and helplessness when even she couldn't keep up her usual smirk and attitude. The book would have been so much better if she were the main character. To better convince you of Claire's greatness, I'd like to bring in a snippet of conversation between Claire(the babysitter) and her Taleh (the baby).<br /><i>“So you would literally take a bullet for me.”<br />“No,” Claire said, with zero emotion.<br />“No?” Claire's Taleh said, surprised at her answer.<br />Claire rolled her eyes, annoyed that she had to answer. “If I have time to stand in the way of a bullet, you have time to move.” </i><br /><br />And I love Bex, the youngest sibling among the Ryels. He's adorable, obedient, caring and helpful, but unfortunately these qualities allow him to be trampled all over by Jared and used too often. I hope that one day in the third book he wakes up to realize what a jerk Jared has been to him.<br /><br />All strengths and weaknesses considered, I have to admit I'm hooked to the series - and dying to know what happens next. I'll be picking up the third book in the very near future, no doubt.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5323416329188777819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Nina and Jared discover she is part of a prophecy that could upset the delicate balance between Heaven and Hell.   <span id="freeText15296894936303510396" style="display:none"> 4.5 Stars<br /> “Requiem” picks up right where “Providence” leaves off.<br /> Nina and Jared are together and having dealt with the challenges left behind by her father following her death. Nina and Jared discover she is part of a prophecy that could upset the delicate balance between Heaven and Hell. The question becomes how to protect Nina and still run her Dad’s company and plan her wedding to Jared.<br /> Very surprisingly I thought this sequel was better than “Providence”…not something I find happening very often, for sure.<br /> Requiem still has all the mystery, romance, action and adventure of “Providence”, but the characters have grown so much since the last book. My only complaint would be that Nina is a bit “slow” in this book…it could be all the sleep-deprivation she is experiencing. There were times when the answer to a question was quite obvious, but Nina just couldn’t or wouldn’t grasp it. <br /> Can’t wait for the next installment! <br /></span>

  <span id="freeText13230867832153089915" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars!***</b><br /><br />Still good, but not as good as the first book. Sometimes it was overly dramatic but it was balanced with cute, mushy scenes.<br /><br />Nina and Jared are stronger than ever. With Ryan gone in an army, Jared doesn't have a rival anymore and he doesn't feel so afraid and teritorial anymore. But there are other problems. Nina can't sleep because her dreams are filled with her dead father dying over and over again.<br /><br />There is a book out there, but it is belong to a devil himself. And they have to get it. Because without it Nina's life might be in danger.<br /><br />Sometimes I felt like some dramatic scenes were too forced.     <a title="Jessica Buwalda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6926261-jessica-buwalda"><img alt="Jessica Buwalda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600119200p2/6926261.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/333901295?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica Buwalda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica Buwalda" href="/user/show/6926261-jessica-buwalda">Jessica Buwalda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer333901295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15364601193500735854">Ok. So I loved the first one and I still love Jared and Nina in this one. In fact I’m starting to really appreciate and love all the characters in this novel. However, Jamie McGuire has stepped outside of just Angels and Demons and into religion in this novel. I’m a little scared to read the next one because when it comes to religion it’s generally a subject that I think writers should try to avoid or tread lightly. I know, I know. How can you someone write about angels and demons but not write </span>
  <span id="freeText15364601193500735854" style="display:none">Ok. So I loved the first one and I still love Jared and Nina in this one. In fact I’m starting to really appreciate and love all the characters in this novel. However, Jamie McGuire has stepped outside of just Angels and Demons and into religion in this novel. I’m a little scared to read the next one because when it comes to religion it’s generally a subject that I think writers should try to avoid or tread lightly. I know, I know. How can you someone write about angels and demons but not write about religion but some manage to...her first book did. So I’m just a bit hesitant t continue. If you’ve read the book you probably understand the exact part of this novel that I’m referring to. <br />Anyhow, religion aside I still loved the book. I loved the characters, even though Nina was a lot crankier in this novel but I guess getting 4 hours of sleep a night would do that to you. Not to mention the life style they live. And once again McGuire did have me on the edge of my seat saying “No, no, no. Please don’t let that happen.” She does know how to tug on your heartstrings.<br />Not to mention I was ecstatic when something I predicted in the first novel actually happens in the second (mainly Ryan’s involvement in everything). Now if only my predications about why Bex can sense demons and others more than the others comes to I will be set and laughing my evil laugh.<br />Good:<br />Nina: She’s finally learning to stop standing behind Jared and stand with him. She can somewhat kick butt too. A little<br />Jared: As always sexy, protective. Sigh.<br />Ryan: I’m really starting to enjoy Ryan now. In the first novel I thought he was annoying and should just move out of the way. Not so much anymore. Not to mention this kid ends up in the hospital a lot!<br />Claire: She’s starting to relax. And I’m starting to like her<br />Bex: You crafty little bugger you. You’re going to end up being the strongest and greatest of the siblings aren’t you? And probably for good reason.<br />Bad: <br />I kind of got a whole Twilight feeling about this series. Mainly the love triangle and why Nina and Ryan were actually close in the first place. Not to mention what I think will happen in the next book with Bex. Feeling a little twilightly. That and the religion thing. I hope she treads lightly and doesn’t do anything too drastic with religion in the next book. It tends to be a touchy subject with a lot of people.<br /><br />View more of my review and others at my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.mynotsovacantshelf.blogspot.com">www.mynotsovacantshelf.blogspot.com</a></span>

<div id="review_258916803" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/258916803" />
    <a title="Sue Tint" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4544187-sue-tint"><img alt="Sue Tint" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294234369p2/4544187.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/258916803?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue Tint" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue Tint" href="/user/show/4544187-sue-tint">Sue Tint</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">lovers of romance and action</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer258916803" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12455795862709314462">Better than its predecessor and a lot of fun!<br/>4.5 stars<br/><br/>Requiem is the second book in the planned Providence trilogy by self-published author, Jamie McGuire. While I thoroughly enjoyed Providence, I think this second installment is even better than its predecessor. <br/><br/>Requiem picks up right where Providence left off. Nina has been recuperating from an injury sustained at the end of Providence, that the love of her life, and protector, Jared could not protect her from. In addition to that, Nina has be</span>
  <span id="freeText12455795862709314462" style="display:none">Better than its predecessor and a lot of fun!<br />4.5 stars<br /><br />Requiem is the second book in the planned Providence trilogy by self-published author, Jamie McGuire. While I thoroughly enjoyed Providence, I think this second installment is even better than its predecessor. <br /><br />Requiem picks up right where Providence left off. Nina has been recuperating from an injury sustained at the end of Providence, that the love of her life, and protector, Jared could not protect her from. In addition to that, Nina has been having horrible nightmares about the death of her father, Jack. However, Nina soon learns that there is a reason for the nightmares, Jack and his own guardian and protector, Gabe, are trying to tell her something. <br /><br />While Providence was about Nina discovering Jared and (quickly) falling in love, Requiem is a continuation of their love, and of their story, and the reason for Nina needing protection. Providence was a little slow for me, I found myself waiting and waiting for something to happen. Requiem was loaded with much more action, mysteries presented and revealed. It was much more fast paced. <br /><br />The "twists" and mysteries that were revealed, I feel could have been revealed in a slower manner, or perhaps with a bit more mystery behind them. It was almost too quick how we would learn a secret about a character, out of the blue. I would have liked a little bit more intrigue than what we were given.<br /><br />The highlights of this book, as with Providence (and McGuire's awesome Beautiful Disaster) come from McGuire's characters and the way she develops the relationships between them. I absolutely love Nina and Jared as a couple. He is her protector, true, but his love for her is so palpable in McGuire's writing, that I felt I could feel the emotions that they (literally) share. McGuire definitely knows how to write about relationships and the dialog is spot on. I really enjoyed this book and am sad that I have to wait a couple of months for the 3rd and final installment. I remain impressed that a self-published author can turn out such great quality books. Thanks Jamie! </span>
  <a data-text-id="12455795862709314462" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/186610505?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tough Critic Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tough Critic Book Reviews" href="/user/show/5336035-tough-critic-book-reviews">Tough Critic Book Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer186610505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15115513981851767072">Jamie McGuire is 3 for 3, another great read. After reading Providence, I could not wait for the sequel. Requiem did not disappoint. I loved the addition of Bex as a main character; his angel side is mature way beyond his years while his human side is your typical 13 year old boy. It was also great to see Nina throw away her damsel in distress title and get in the fight. Jared also changes in that he stands his ground alot more with Nina. In Providence, I made the comment that sometimes Jared ap</span>
  <span id="freeText15115513981851767072" style="display:none">Jamie McGuire is 3 for 3, another great read. After reading Providence, I could not wait for the sequel. Requiem did not disappoint. I loved the addition of Bex as a main character; his angel side is mature way beyond his years while his human side is your typical 13 year old boy. It was also great to see Nina throw away her damsel in distress title and get in the fight. Jared also changes in that he stands his ground alot more with Nina. In Providence, I made the comment that sometimes Jared appears to be a little whipped; in Requiem he does not succumb to Nina's every want and whim. He actually is pretty stubborn and stands his ground if he feels that what he's doing is in her best interest. Overall a great read. My only complaint was that the plot got a little too far out there at times and there was almost too much going on. It also moved quite fast; I don't mean that as a negative aspect of the book, but I blinked and Sophomore year was over. <br /><br />I absolutely love these characters especially Nina and Jared. Their relationship is full of mind...no, heart blowing romance!!! My favorite part of this book has to be the direction and development she took with her characters. Though I didn't think it was possible, I loved them even more the second time around. This is a great series that I highly recomend. Can't wait for book 3 :-)</span>
  <a data-text-id="15115513981851767072" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer472725570" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1159684869148034484"><strong>2.5 stars</strong><br/><br/>Much better than the original - though Im not sure if that means anything. I doubt I would have bothered to read this if I hadn't gotten the entire trilogy on Kindle for $2.99, bc I really thought the 1st book was awful.<br/><br/>There was a real plot this time, and it was actually fairly interesting, if not exactly original. It helped that the book wasn't 100% focused on the "romance" between Jared and Nina, as that has got to be one of the creepiest, most boring love stories in YA Wannabe Land.</span>
  <span id="freeText1159684869148034484" style="display:none"><strong>2.5 stars</strong><br /><br />Much better than the original - though Im not sure if that means anything. I doubt I would have bothered to read this if I hadn't gotten the entire trilogy on Kindle for $2.99, bc I really thought the 1st book was awful.<br /><br />There was a real plot this time, and it was actually fairly interesting, if not exactly original. It helped that the book wasn't 100% focused on the "romance" between Jared and Nina, as that has got to be one of the creepiest, most boring love stories in YA Wannabe Land. <br /><br />However, I have one humongous complaint: Have these people never heard of condoms? You just been told that you might create a baby that will upset the balance between heaven and hell, and you want to use <strong>
  <i>the rhythm method??</i>
</strong> What is this, 1952?<br /><br />Some well placed commas and not capitalizing 'sweetheart','dear' and 'son' would really go a long way to making the writing far less flat and clunky. (Isn't that Grammar 101??) Even so, it was still better than Providence. I hope Ms. McGuire has invested in an editor for her later books.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18262917524153446220">Eeehhhh....I don't really know how to rate this-It wasn't good and it wasn't bad. It was just..ok-and that makes me sad becuase after the first, I figured the intensity would only pick up. Instead, it goes into great detail about Nina's history and the history of...well....I suppose religion? I wouldn't know because suffice to say, I skimmed at least 50% of this novel-I know, tsk tsk. I just couldn't get into the story. Which sucks. A lot. <br/><br/>I love Claire, and I love Jared. I even love Ryan(now), </span>
  <span id="freeText18262917524153446220" style="display:none">Eeehhhh....I don't really know how to rate this-It wasn't good and it wasn't bad. It was just..ok-and that makes me sad becuase after the first, I figured the intensity would only pick up. Instead, it goes into great detail about Nina's history and the history of...well....I suppose religion? I wouldn't know because suffice to say, I skimmed at least 50% of this novel-I know, tsk tsk. I just couldn't get into the story. Which sucks. A lot. <br><br>I love Claire, and I love Jared. I even love Ryan(now), but even these great characters couldn't save this heavy-in-religious-history novel. I just felt bored the whole time. Near the end I will give it kudos, because all of Nina's dreams finally seem to come in handy when the action ensues-brief, but thorough action. <br><br>Lastly, I am going to say I don't know why there is so much love for this Kim character. I disliked her in the first and I loathed her in the second. She is a very obnoxious, in-your-face annoying character. Just because she is a little in the know in the second does not give her more of a right to be even snarkier. That's all I will say on her character.<br><br>All in all an ok novel, just not really a novel I would recommend to those around me. If it weren't for Jared I doubt I would finish the third and final installment in the series, but I am an avid reader through and through, and I will finish this series...eventually. I would rather start others on my TBR list before I come back to Eden, which says a lot :/ I never separate series if I don't have to. Some will love it, some will hate it-guess you'll have to read to figure out which one of those categories you are.<br><br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews visit<br><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"><img height="240" width="385" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407869528i/10772466._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> </i></span>

<div id="review_275419973" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/275419973" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4979538-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520654483p2/4979538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/275419973?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/4979538-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4979538-erin?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4979538-erin?shelf=pnr-faves">pnr-faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer275419973" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer273345254883734724">Okay, so Jamie McGuire clearly decided to branch out with Requiem and try to take on something different. Beautiful Disaster was an amazingly touching love story and Providence took an all-encompasing love and threw it in the middle of some dark and mysterious events. I was curious to see how the romance in Providence would play out in Requiem without growing tired, but Jamie took me completely by surprise!! Requiem isn't just a continuation of this unforgettable love story that I fell head over</span>
  <span id="freeText273345254883734724" style="display:none">Okay, so Jamie McGuire clearly decided to branch out with Requiem and try to take on something different. Beautiful Disaster was an amazingly touching love story and Providence took an all-encompasing love and threw it in the middle of some dark and mysterious events. I was curious to see how the romance in Providence would play out in Requiem without growing tired, but Jamie took me completely by surprise!! Requiem isn't just a continuation of this unforgettable love story that I fell head over heels for, in fact I feel like it was the polar opposite of Providence. Whereas Providence had Nina and Jared's steamy whirlwind romance with a slight threat of danger lurking in the background, Requiem throws all of the characters into the dead center of all the danger, to the point that there's little time for anything else. It was not at all what I expected, but I really think Jamie's choice paid off for this series!<br /><br />Requiem finds Nina plagued by terrifying nightmares where Gabe and Jack are repeatedly being killed as she watches. Jared feels helpless to do something to help her, and she in the meantime is finding it more and more difficult to function. It was so sad to read about Nina literally just falling apart from endless nights with no sleep thanks to her dreams, and as the book goes on they got downright creepy. We're talking exorcist scene, crawling up the walls, creepy!! *shutters* WIth Claire protecting Ryan overseas, Jared and Bex are left to protect Nina and figure out a solution to her dreams on their own. Everywhere they turn they hit a dead end, and there doesn't seem to be a light at the end of the tunnel. When events force Ryan to return home and Claire can finally help, they discover that Nina is destined to play a pivotal role in the battle of good vs. evil. They set off to fight the evil forces to find the one book that may hold some answers, but it may not be enough; Nina may have to carry out her role, changing everything. <br /><br />There was a LOT going on in the second half of this book, between new discoveries, the family secret threatening to be exposed to another, and the constant fight with their enemies. Jared and company find themselves having to recover from massive injuries on several occasions, which had me cringing. I didn't like reading that these characters I love so much were suffering! It definitely showed how strong and amazing the Ryels are, though, and I just so adore them! I did miss the steaminess between Nina and Jared, but I think it was great to see what was behind the danger that was eluded to in Providence. I wanted to slap Nina at times for dwelling on Ryan more than a devoted fiance of a super-sexy half-angel should be, but I LOVE the way Jamie has it panning out for the series. It all makes sense and brings things back full-circle. The ending of Requiem comes with a big bomb being dropped for Nina and Jared, and I so look forward to getting my hands on my copy of Eden in the mail!! Great series!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="273345254883734724" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_587827705" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/587827705" />
    <a title="Sarahjane Larkin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7294263-sarahjane-larkin"><img alt="Sarahjane Larkin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338841165p2/7294263.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/587827705?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarahjane Larkin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarahjane Larkin" href="/user/show/7294263-sarahjane-larkin">Sarahjane Larkin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer587827705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13145298965569931121">Dreaming of the dead might mean a restless night for anyone, but for Nina Grey it was a warning.<br/><br/>Still healing from her last run-in with Hell, Nina struggles with not only her life as a Brown University student, but also as an intern at Titan Shipping, her father's company. Recurring nightmares about her father's violent death have become a nightly event, but being overwhelmed with guilt from Ryan's unexpected departure to the Armed Forces, and heart ache over Claire being across the ocean to pro</span>
  <span id="freeText13145298965569931121" style="display:none">Dreaming of the dead might mean a restless night for anyone, but for Nina Grey it was a warning.<br /><br />Still healing from her last run-in with Hell, Nina struggles with not only her life as a Brown University student, but also as an intern at Titan Shipping, her father's company. Recurring nightmares about her father's violent death have become a nightly event, but being overwhelmed with guilt from Ryan's unexpected departure to the Armed Forces, and heart ache over Claire being across the ocean to protect him, Nina believes her sleepless nights are the least of her problems—but she's wrong.<br /><br />Worried about Nina's declining health, Jared must steal back Shax's book for answers. Fighting new enemies, and with the help of new friends, Jared's worst fear comes to fruition. Desperate, he is faced with a choice: Fight Hell alone, or start a war with Heaven.<br /><br /> *****<br /><br />Book two...if you’ve read the first book based on the above, Well done. You’ve made an excellent choice. If you’re reading this because your still not sure, well be warned, this will contain a whole lot of spoilers. <br /><br />Unlike Providence, Requiem is set over a much longer period of time, mainly due to the plot. The first book was about the foundations of setting up this relationship, and this book is about the consequences of going against fate in such a way. <br /><br />Nina and Jared, are a couple against all odds and against fate, however the truth about Nina’s father’s final actions are only just beginning to come to light. With Nina working at her father’s company around her studies at College, she’s a pretty busy person. This isn’t helped by the fact that at night, she’s plagued by nightmares of the night her father died, stealing Shax’s book the first time, and the nightmares show no sign of stopping. Which means one thing, they must get the book back.<br /><br />Now one of the strengths of Providence was the relationship between Jared and Nina, and in Requiem, this relationship is tested, not by Ryan or any other characters, but because of the nature of the relationship. There’s a pattern to the nightmares and a reason behind them, a warning. A warning that could mean the end of the relationship or their lives. <br /><br />Now, like I said, this book takes a much larger time span, which works in its favour. The time makes the events much more dire and real, in the readers mind. Yes, McGuire could have taken the option of introducing another conflict, to save her from skipping time and writing about a few months later, but I’m glad she didn’t, because the original conflict is enough, and introducing another would make this messy and confusing. Besides, adding something else to tear this couple apart, would have taken the charm from the characters, and would have seemed like an easy, fools way out.<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4464118.Jamie_McGuire" title="Jamie McGuire" rel="nofollow noopener">Jamie McGuire</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13145298965569931121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_503640918" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/503640918" />
    <a title="Tally" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4661507-tally"><img alt="Tally" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296778534p2/4661507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/503640918?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tally" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tally" href="/user/show/4661507-tally">Tally</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4661507-tally?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer503640918" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8376403715016568806">Title: Requiem<br/>Author: Jamie McGuire<br/>Pages: 257(paperback)<br/>Rating: 2/5<br/>Other reviews: Book I<br/><br/>I remember being impressed with the first book so when I saw this in display at the library I couldn’t help but pick it up with some measure of high expectations. Much to my dismay, I found REQUIEM to have suffered greatly from the dreaded middle book syndrome. The synopsis:<br/><br/> Dreaming of the dead might mean a restless night for anyone, but for Nina Grey it was a warning.<br/><br/> Still healing from her last run-in with</span>
  <span id="freeText8376403715016568806" style="display:none">Title: Requiem<br />Author: Jamie McGuire<br />Pages: 257(paperback)<br />Rating: 2/5<br />Other reviews: Book I<br /><br />I remember being impressed with the first book so when I saw this in display at the library I couldn’t help but pick it up with some measure of high expectations. Much to my dismay, I found REQUIEM to have suffered greatly from the dreaded middle book syndrome. The synopsis:<br /><br /> Dreaming of the dead might mean a restless night for anyone, but for Nina Grey it was a warning.<br /><br /> Still healing from her last run-in with Hell, Nina struggles with not only her life as a Brown University student, but also as an intern at Titan Shipping, her father’s company. Recurring nightmares about her father’s violent death have become a nightly event, but being overwhelmed with guilt from Ryan’s unexpected departure to the Armed Forces, and heart ache over Claire being across the ocean to protect him, Nina believes her sleepless nights are the least of her problems—but she’s wrong.<br /><br /> Worried about Nina’s declining health, Jared must steal back Shax’s book for answers. Fighting new enemies, and with the help of new friends, Jared’s worst fear comes to fruition. Desperate, he is faced with a choice: Fight Hell alone, or start a war with Heaven.<br /><br /> Where to start? The romance I so praised in PROVIDENCE has evolved into a sort of given that Jared will be there to protect Nina and they have such a great connection that he seems to read her thoughts. In truth, I found Nina to be a wimp. Several times you’re told that she’ll stop crying. Don’t hold your breath, I do believe she spent most of the time in tears. Or stressed (which may or may not have caused me to feel stressed out myself. Might just be school though, hehe).<br /><br />In book time, McGuire skips through a whole year and not much gets done. In fact, I would daresay nothing in this book happens. Sure they learn about the prophecy foretelling dire things but as a reader I don’t just want to be handed this information. So much potential for some great action scenes but they happen elsewhere while we sit tight with Nina, safe and sound. There were a few times when I was successfully confused with the paranormal things going on or the explanations of them.<br /><br />None of the characters stood out this time. New or old. Ryan was a little less annoying. The ending was pretty much what I expected, no surprise there. There were some fun moments in the book, I won’t deny that.<br /><br />Overall, REQUIEM didn’t rise to my expectations in any form and I was a little happy to just finish it. Not sure if I’ll be picking up the third book anytime soon, we’ll just have to see.<br /><br />~Tally</span>
  <a data-text-id="8376403715016568806" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9784780015314809793">WORKED UP!! yes, that's how i feel. its like the whole book is full of intense emotions that i can't seem to find the right words to describe it. What i strongly feel right now (after finishing the book just a few minutes ago) is the need to get to the next book. haha. Well, while the first book is all about falling in love and has a lot of sweet scenes, the second one is all about keeping the relationship and facing odds. The characters definitely have all grown up. Claire still being the spunk</span>
  <span id="freeText9784780015314809793" style="display:none">WORKED UP!! yes, that's how i feel. its like the whole book is full of intense emotions that i can't seem to find the right words to describe it. What i strongly feel right now (after finishing the book just a few minutes ago) is the need to get to the next book. haha. Well, while the first book is all about falling in love and has a lot of sweet scenes, the second one is all about keeping the relationship and facing odds. The characters definitely have all grown up. Claire still being the spunky bad ass that i've known her to be but quite nice now to Nina, Bex being the good protective teenage mutant.. or should i say spiderman/superman wannabe?, Jared being more protective and less melodramatic, Nina shows a lot of strength in the second book, i guess? since she's the one experiencing lack of sleep and a lot of internal turmoil, i guess she's entitled to a little bit of credit even if she's not really facing the bad guys head on (literally). I like it that Claire would end up with Ryan.. i don't see an end to Nina's guilt where he's concerned vanishing anytime soon if the author didn't make Ryan fall for Claire. I have to say, i never saw Kim coming. I was totally shocked. I even thought Kim had a thing for Ryan back in book one and in the first few chapters of book two. Ryan also surprised me.. joining the military and then falling for Claire? shocker. But i guess it all worked out for them.<br /><br />The whole prophecy thing was kinda confusing to me, and then when i got the gist.. i feel like its LEGION all over again. Well, i didn't read the book but i watched the film, and its similar somehow. This is just better because the hero is the father of the child haha, just saying.<br /><br />Anyway... collectively, with regards the whole book..its perfect! yes..its a perfect novel for me since it has all the aspects i am looking for. Love, friendship, action, lots of kisses and gunshots here and there ^_^.<br /><br />Looking forward to the next book. =)<br /><br /><br />oh and by the way.. ever noticed that Ryan keeps on getting himself hospitalized? just a thought..</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11176054016670780260"><a href='http://jessicasbookreview.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Read more reviews on my blog</a> | <a href='https://www.facebook.com/JessicasBookReview' rel='nofollow noopener'>Like me on Facebook</a><br/><br/>Requiem is the second book in the trilogy Providence by Jamie McGuire. The book pretty much picks up where Providence left off. <br/><br/>Nina and Jared are happy, playing house living together in his loft. The demons are still after them but things have cooled down a lot. Nina begins having dreams of her dead father and Jared's dead father telling her to find the book and she is the one. The dreams, I should say nightmares keep her up and the lack of slee</span>
  <span id="freeText11176054016670780260" style="display:none"><a href="http://jessicasbookreview.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Read more reviews on my blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/JessicasBookReview" rel="nofollow noopener">Like me on Facebook</a><br /><br />Requiem is the second book in the trilogy Providence by Jamie McGuire. The book pretty much picks up where Providence left off. <br /><br />Nina and Jared are happy, playing house living together in his loft. The demons are still after them but things have cooled down a lot. Nina begins having dreams of her dead father and Jared's dead father telling her to find the book and she is the one. The dreams, I should say nightmares keep her up and the lack of sleep is starting to get to her school work and life. Ryan who lost Nina to Jared leaves for the army and Claire is forced to go with him to protect him since she is now his Guardian Angel.<br /><br />Nina's dreams are more vivid as time goes on and Jared is trying to search for the meaning of her dreams. As time goes on, Sophomore year ends (It is stars and ends so quickly, almost too quickly). As the story goes on, more information about Demons comes out and I sometimes thought it was too much. I was getting really confused with the different levels and who was who. A lot of named are mentioned throughout the story. I really enjoyed Providence book 1 but thought book 2 was a little over the top at moments and went by really quickly. Nina is an Jr. now in the book studying at Brown but also works as CEO in her father's company, has a fiance, and is trying to find a book. I didn't really understand how one girl could be in charge with so much at a time.<br /><br />I again enjoyed the relationship with Nina &amp; Jared. He is pretty amazing and a new fictional boyfriend of mine :) I did not enjoy it as much as the first one but it is still a 4 star novel and I will jumping into book 3 next!</span>

  <span id="freeText7969705725183196005" style="display:none">What can I say about Requiem that would do it justice....... HOLY NEPHILIM!!!!!!!!!! Jamie you are incredible!<br /><br />Requiem picks up right where Providence left off. Nina and Jared have survived the worse. Nina is healed from the shot out she was in and Jared is more protective of her. Nina is still reeling over the information she has learned about her father. Now she is caught up in a cat and mouse game with demons who want the book her father stole.<br /><br />Jared will do anything to keep Nina safe from the demons so he keeps his eyes on her. She lives her normal life but after school she stays with him. Only Nina needs answers and so she goes in search of them and what she finds is not what she expected. Jared is very worried about Nina because she is now exposed to his world and sometimes the people in his world can be worse then the demons.<br /><br />And if life was not hard enough as is Nina has to deal with Ryan's romantic advances. She loves him but just as a friend and nothing more. He makes it unbearable sometimes because he has made it quite clear he loves her and he is not going down without a fight. The only thing is he underestimated Jared's love for Nina.<br /><br />What will Nina do when she is faced with the truth? Will she run to Jared or will she chose the safe road of Ryan? Come along for the ride of a lifetime with Nina and Jared and the gang. This is a must read series that will knock you off your feet!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16411778902001343458">What an awesome read. Jamie McGuire continues to impress me with her talent. She is a very gifted author. I am absolutely convinced she can write anything and it would be amazing. I have now read a contemporary romance and two paranormal romances by her. She shifts between the two different genres with ease and grace. I recently found out from visiting her website that she plans to write a book about Zombies. There truly isn’t anything Jamie McGuire can’t do. She is phenomenal and now one of my </span>
  <span id="freeText16411778902001343458" style="display:none">What an awesome read. Jamie McGuire continues to impress me with her talent. She is a very gifted author. I am absolutely convinced she can write anything and it would be amazing. I have now read a contemporary romance and two paranormal romances by her. She shifts between the two different genres with ease and grace. I recently found out from visiting her website that she plans to write a book about Zombies. There truly isn’t anything Jamie McGuire can’t do. She is phenomenal and now one of my favorite authors.<br /><br />I enjoyed everything about this book. This book is packed full of everything any reader could want. It has a beautifully written romance and on the edge of your seat action and suspense. <br /><br />What I enjoyed most besides the romantic aspect of the book is the tight knit family. The Ryel’s are a family anyone would be proud to be a part of. They would go to the ends of the earth for one another literally. It is sweet and enduring. When I finished I found myself in a bit of mourning. I didn’t want to give up being with this family and rich storyline. <br /><br />This truly is stellar book and phenomenal series. I am dying to know what happens in book three. I recently spoke to the author and she is half way through with completing Eden. I will be on pins and needles while I wait for it to be released.<br /><br />A huge thank you goes out to my good friend Jennifer for buddy reading this with me. It has been a fun ride and I am happy we were able to share it together. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_483158968" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/483158968" />
    <a title="Tiffany" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7571542-tiffany"><img alt="Tiffany" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542787877p2/7571542.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/483158968?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tiffany" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tiffany" href="/user/show/7571542-tiffany">Tiffany</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7571542-tiffany?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer483158968" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4379595450796694528">Well, I stared and finished book two all in one day. First off, I actually didn't enjoy most of this book, but I was attached to characters enough from the first book to keep me going. It wasn't boring, or necessarily bad, it was just nothing like book one. This biggest difference was that while book one had just the right amount of supernatural surrounding a cute love story that had some edge of your seat action, book two was ALLLLLLLLLLLL paranormal! Which brings me to why I didn't like most o</span>
  <span id="freeText4379595450796694528" style="display:none">Well, I stared and finished book two all in one day. First off, I actually didn't enjoy most of this book, but I was attached to characters enough from the first book to keep me going. It wasn't boring, or necessarily bad, it was just nothing like book one. This biggest difference was that while book one had just the right amount of supernatural surrounding a cute love story that had some edge of your seat action, book two was ALLLLLLLLLLLL paranormal! Which brings me to why I didn't like most of this book. This book had WAY WAY WAY too much paranormal in it for me to just jump on board the believe-and-go-with-it train. It was super dark and twisty too, almost horror story like at times, like I was reading some kind of messed up bible between all the heaven and hell history and then the dark and twisty scary touch to the story. That being said, WHAT AND END!!! For the last maybe 70 pages, or something like that, this book had talked me into giving it 4 stars like the first book, but yeah...no...after thinking on it, it's just not as good as the first so it really deserves to have 3. My original 4 star thoughts are probably just because I'm attached to the characters. The bottom line on this one is that the first book is definitely better.......we seem to have gone off some crazy paranormal deep end. I shall continue though! Eden here I come, please be more like book one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4379595450796694528" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/318687700?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2012</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11691400-requiem">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8837962-lucia?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8837962-lucia?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer318687700" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer274320528778365">OMG, this book was amazing! Usually, middle book in the series is not as good as first or last part. But Requiem definitely does not fall within this cathegory. I loved everything about this book, every single twist, every single moment, every single turn out. And most importantly, I love Jamie McGuire's style of writing. This series are becoming my absolutely most favourite paranoraml stories of all time. I cannot wait to find out what will happen in last part. <br/><br/>Requiem is a little bit different</span>
  <span id="freeText274320528778365" style="display:none">OMG, this book was amazing! Usually, middle book in the series is not as good as first or last part. But Requiem definitely does not fall within this cathegory. I loved everything about this book, every single twist, every single moment, every single turn out. And most importantly, I love Jamie McGuire's style of writing. This series are becoming my absolutely most favourite paranoraml stories of all time. I cannot wait to find out what will happen in last part. <br /><br />Requiem is a little bit different comparing to Providence, but it is equally good. Beginning of the book was depressing, Nina and Jared had to face more problems, more fears, more worries so romantic scenes were put into the background in Requiem. But it was all compensated with plenty of action so I did not have a time to even think about missing some loving scenes. <br /><br />Beside the neverstoping action ride, book offers deeper insides into the individual characters and into Heaven-Eart-Hell relations. And of course, we got to read some more beautiful words from Jared :) <br /><br />Well, I could not put this book down. It is really good. All I can do is to recommend it to all paranormal stories lovers - do not hesitate and read this series as soon as possible.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer745676041" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1786986584938128965">I'm really torn between 2.5 and 3.5 stars. The numerous misspellings and grammatical errors were excruciating, they were at every turn as if they were a supporting character!<br/><br/>I still love Jared and found myself absolutely adoring Bex while warming up to Ryan and Claire. But ohmigod, Nina made me want to slam my head against a wall! She was so needy and clingy and whiny and STUPID! She literally gave herself pep talks on being strong and not crying continuously throughout the book, which was a com</span>
  <span id="freeText1786986584938128965" style="display:none">I'm really torn between 2.5 and 3.5 stars. The numerous misspellings and grammatical errors were excruciating, they were at every turn as if they were a supporting character!<br /><br />I still love Jared and found myself absolutely adoring Bex while warming up to Ryan and Claire. But ohmigod, Nina made me want to slam my head against a wall! She was so needy and clingy and whiny and STUPID! She literally gave herself pep talks on being strong and not crying continuously throughout the book, which was a complete waste of time because if this was a wimpy, whiny, tear-streaked competition she would tie with Bella Swan. I had my doubts about her character in the first book but, this 2nd installment almost pushed me over the edge; hell I contemplated giving up on the book several times because Nina was so infuriating. <br /><br />But I digress, this book had one purpose: to arm us with enough information to tackle the last book.<br /><br />There's romance, but very little of it.<br />There's action, but very little of it.<br />There's a twist (if you can call it that), but of course very, very little of it.<br /><br />This book is a means to an end and nothing more.</span>

          </span>

    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WOxMxjKtMFYdDAg9t7kJ1BSD4sUtd+vIySDNT/jAeu9O9U/PqJHBBZBfzkg6IZkILQJImbATNYCi3K7bBHNVoA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VmJ9wDGqqtFjv8mkiIEbmPfjLh5sgfC7cZmy8SlFVrJAe37Jq5Zbgu7sD9EFGYtEzmKEQvHlLvMaZdFl1fZ5/Q==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4464118.Jamie_McGuire">About Jamie McGuire</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/4464118.Jamie_McGuire"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1539783525p3/4464118.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/4464118.Jamie_McGuire">Jamie McGuire

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6060660595111515062">Jamie McGuire was born in Tulsa, Oklahoma. She attended Northern Oklahoma College, the University of Central Oklahoma, and Autry Technology Center where she graduated with a degree in Radiography.<br/><br/>Jamie paved the way for the New Adult genre with the international bestseller Beautiful Disaster. Her follow-up novel, Walking Disaster, debuted at #1 on the New York Times, USA Today, and Wall Street Jou</span>
  <span id="freeText6060660595111515062" style="display:none">Jamie McGuire was born in Tulsa, Oklahoma. She attended Northern Oklahoma College, the University of Central Oklahoma, and Autry Technology Center where she graduated with a degree in Radiography.<br /><br />Jamie paved the way for the New Adult genre with the international bestseller Beautiful Disaster. Her follow-up novel, Walking Disaster, debuted at #1 on the New York Times, USA Today, and Wall Street Journal bestseller lists in all four categories. Beautiful Oblivion, book one of the Maddox Brothers series, also topped the New York Times bestseller list, debuting at #1. In 2015, books two and three of the Maddox Brothers series, Beautiful Redemption and Beautiful Sacrifice, respectively, also topped the New York Times, as well as a Beautiful series novella, Something Beautiful. In 2016, Beautiful Burn made an appearance on the New York Times and USA Today, and was also named iBooks' Romance Book of the Year. The same year, A Beautiful Funeral also topped the New York Times bestseller list.<br /><br />Novels also written by Jamie McGuire include: apocalyptic thriller and 2014 UtopYA Best Dystopian Book of the Year, Red Hill; the Providence series, a young adult paranormal romance trilogy; Apolonia, a dark sci-fi romance; and several novellas, including A Beautiful Wedding, Among Monsters, Happenstance: A Novella Series, and Sins of the Innocent.<br /><br />Jamie is the first indie author in history to strike a print deal with retail giant Wal-Mart. Her self-published novel, Beautiful Redemption hit Wal-Mart shelves in September, 2015.<br /><br />Jamie lives in Steamboat Springs, Colorado with her husband, Jeff, and their three children. <br /><br />Find Jamie at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jamiemcguire.com">www.jamiemcguire.com</a> or on Facebook, Twitter, Google +, and Instagram.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6060660595111515062" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
